Where SAT Has Gone Wrong (or Remains Unresolved):
	1.	Filament Geometry Ambiguity
	‚Ä¢	Core entities (filaments) remain structurally underdefined. The model hasn‚Äôt settled on whether they are helices, braids, ribbons, or something else. This undermines reproducibility of SAT-based mass or interaction predictions, particularly when twist state mapping is involved.
	2.	Œ∏‚ÇÑ Cause vs. Effect Ambiguity
	‚Ä¢	It‚Äôs still unclear whether Œ∏‚ÇÑ is a driving field (i.e., a force-generating quantity) or an emergent descriptor of filament orientation. If it‚Äôs emergent, using it as a Lagrangian field variable may be conceptually inverted.
	3.	Quantization Not Implemented
	‚Ä¢	SAT remains a classical theory. There‚Äôs no Fock space, no operator algebra, no canonical quantization or path integral. Without this, SAT cannot make standard quantum predictions or interface with QFT or SM at the level of particle behavior.
	4.	Wavefront Ontology Underdeveloped
	‚Ä¢	Is the wavefront a propagating energy boundary? A metaphysical timesheet? A brane-like excitation? The answer vacillates. Until this is formalized, gravitational, cosmological, and decoherence-related implications are speculative.
	5.	Mass Hierarchy Still Ad Hoc
	‚Ä¢	Although SAT elegantly proposes mass as angular drag (via sin¬≤Œ∏‚ÇÑ), it has not yet yielded predictive mass ratios except through symbolic post-fits (e.g., Œº:e ‚âà œÄ‚Åµ ¬± Œµ). There's no generative model for spacing or family replication.
	6.	Coordinate Invariance Problem
	‚Ä¢	SAT lacks manifest coordinate invariance. It presumes a preferred frame (wavefront surface), which is at odds with GR. Without reformulating in a covariant framework, coupling to gravity or ensuring frame-consistent predictions is precarious.
	7.	Œ∏‚ÇÑ Measurability Remains Vague
	‚Ä¢	It‚Äôs the central variable, but Œ∏‚ÇÑ has no clear proxy in experimental data‚Äîno device or observable that directly measures angular deviation from a propagating time wavefront. The refractive index link is suggestive but insufficiently resolved.
	8.	Most Empirical Predictions Still Weak
	‚Ä¢	Attempts at predicting Œ± drift, anomalous optical behaviors, or polarization effects have mostly yielded inconclusive or statistically insignificant matches. Some proposed retrodictions are promising but require re-analysis of historical datasets with new criteria.
